I think a lot of people don't understand how cancer works. It spreads throughout the organs, if we are talking about the 4th stage, and affects the surrounding tissues. In the case of pancreatic cancer, this is usually the liver, kidneys, lungs, bones, and gastrointestinal tract. If it has developed like this in half a year, then this is a case of a very VERY aggressive tumor (there are several types). At some point, the growing tumor begins to decompose, that is, as if in place of the pancreas, a zone of necrotic tissue is formed, plus the fact that enzymes are produced in the pancreas that dissolve proteins and other products in the stomach can enter the abdominal cavity, plus the affected organs. .. At some point there is simply nothing left to treat, to remove... This is terrible, I feel very sorry for Paul, I don‚Äôt even know how to express it in words. I grew up "religious" attending church frequently, and was in fact a youth minister in my church as an older teenager.  However, I was a complete hypocrite,  living a licentious life, committing the very sins that I condemned publicly from a platform.  You see, that is all I was, "religious".   I believed the lie that my entrance into Eternal Life was based upon my merit and following a set of standards.   I knew privately though that I was a sinner destined for Hell, but always thought that one day I would "straighten up."   For many years I lived a life of complete wickedness and debauchery, hopeful (but not confident) that I had enough "religion" to get me into Heaven.  It was on the aforementioned date that the grace and love of the Lord Jesus became real to me.  I was in a very low place, deservedly so because of all the bad decisions I had made.  Now, I knew the Bible, I had just never made any personal application, trusting instead on morality and good works to secure my place in Heaven.  That is the very essence of "religion", that we deserve or earn everlasting life based upon performing a set of good acts.  However, I knew in my heart that I could never be good enough, and even if I cleaned myself up somehow, what about all of my past wickedness?  As I pondered these thoughts, the Bible became real to me, as for the first time as I understood this:  Rom 5:8 KJV - 8 But God (proved) his love toward us, in that, while we were yet sinners, Christ died for us.  Jesus did not die for me because I am deserving, He did it simply out a of passion to have me live with Him in His house for eternity!   No doubt, you sir are a better person than myself, but the Lord has exacting qualifications as to who is worthy to come into His house.  The Lord is Holy, and will not allow a fraction of a percentage of sin into Heaven, as it would defile Him to do so.   A solution was necessary, as none of us could hope to attain to the perfect standard set by Jesus, the Son of God.   That solution was for Christ to come and die in our place, taking the punishment for our transgressions.   It is a true historical fact that Christ died on the Cross for our sins, and that three days later He rose again.  Because the penalty for sin has been paid for by the precious, divine blood of Jesus, we too can have hope of eternal life.   The payment for all the sins of mankind has been made, all we need do is believe and accept it.  We can add nothing to it by our own puny efforts, as Christ paid it all when He cried out "It is Finished!".   I was, and still am, a big failure in many aspects of my life.   The good news is that my sins have been forgiven, washed clean by the Blood of Jesus!  1Jo 1:7-9 KJV - 7 But if we walk in the light, as he is in the light, we have fellowship one with another, and the blood of Jesus Christ his Son cleanseth us from all sin. 8 If we say that we have no sin, we deceive ourselves, and the truth is not in us. 9 If we confess our sins, he is faithful and just to forgive us [our] sins, and to cleanse us from all unrighteousness. I've watched your channel since 2020 (the "beer" situation spurred me to learn about firearms) and I have gleaned a lot of valuable information from it. Having set out on a mission to provide "real firearms information for citizens", I would say that you have more than succeeded. Now that you're leaving, I feel compelled to leave a comment.  Your philosophy of responsible firearms ownership went a long way in shaping my appreciation of the law, the possible consequences of carrying a gun for personal protection, and the importance of training with professionals who can provide feedback. Much of what my instructors saw, however, was based on my early imitation of your grip and stance, which helped me on my way to developing a style best suited to my body and abilities. I take my self-appointed duties as a personal and family protector quite seriously, and I balance my life and my role as a shield with some of your advice ringing in my mind.   Your presentation of technical information, especially the ammo reviews, has largely steered me away from the boutique cartridges and helped me justify my choice of a .40 S&W full sized pistol for my EDC (and, for some reason, this makes me remember that your bicep is about as big around as a grocery store ham). When I chose to make a snub revolver my pocket pistol, your reviews of .38 SPC ammo also came in really handy.   I took solace from that fact that you, too, "like the classics" (my first centerfire pistol was a Rock Island 1911 that I "accidentally" bought on Gun Broker... my first intentional centerfire pistol was a S&W Model 14-3, with really nice bluing). It's hard to believe that the Beretta 92 is creeping into the classic vintage....  I also derived much entertainment from your holiday specials, the deer that wandered through your range, and treatment of TEOTWAWKI/WROL/ROFL topics... when the world ends, I'll be ready with my preferred rifle/pistol combo.  The presentations that stand out the most for me were your Miami-Dade analysis and the "Can a cop (reliably) shoot a knife out of an assailant's hand?" simulation. I thought they were brilliant.  That brilliance comes from your virtuosic shooting skills. I'm sure I'm not the only new firearms owner who carefully watched how you handled your various firearms, and who aspire to be even half as good as you are.  Well, that's four years of pent up comments and compliments.   No matter what happens in the next few weeks, know that you made a difference in many of your viewer's lives and we are keeping you in our prayers. You took a medium (YouTube) that often scrapes dreadful cultural lows and elevated it to the best it could be: a channel for education, debate, and good (usually) clean entertainment.

Hi Paul. I'm a 71-year-old guy who has been disabled since 2010. That is relevant only because it has given me time to pursue other areas. I focused on my guitar skills and performing folk music shows for several years. By 2018 that ended. Then I rediscovered how much I love shooting. Yours is one of the channels I used to gain the knowledge I didn't have especially with pistols and ammo testing. Your humor is dry like I've been told mine is which is funny given that I was one of our main clinical skills trainers my last decade in the mental health field. Mainly wanted to say thank you. My original rifle and hunting teacher was my Army Sgt dad in rural Arkansas. I guess rural Arkansas is an oxymoron since most of the state is rural. Our area was more backwoods near the Ouachita River in the Ouachita Mtns. It seemed right to have you teaching from an area of the woods that looked a bit like home. I understand the short time and plan to work on my shooting skills with an old buddy of mine until we can't do it any longer. The meat target will remain my favorite target. I even forgive you for not liking my favorite Underwood loads. I am forced to use a 380 due to nerve damage though the new S&W Equalizer allows easier shooting of 9mm. The Underwood Extreme Defender is what I trust in 380 and use in 9mm too. My dad's Winchester Model 94 from the good years remains my deer rifle as I hunt brush. Take care and enjoy what you can as long as you can. That's just what I decided to do. Many close calls in the hospital but still here for now.

In efforts to remember the good times we have had here, I will share the funniest thing to me that I've seen here on Paul's channel. In his most recent intro montage there is a clip of Paul in an old tacky sport coat taking aim with a small snubnosed revolver. The clip comes from one of his testing videos for the best standard pressure .38 special load for self defense where he finds that the old 158 grain lead round nosed bullet performed best. "So if we're going to shoot our grandpa's ammo, we might as well shoot it like he would." And with that Paul wheeles to face the target with a wide, sort of crouched stance with the gun thrust out in front of him. When I saw this from Paul, I burst out laughing. It reminded me of the first time I went to the range with my father after buying my first handgun, a Ruger GP100. After taking a few shots myself, I let my dad have a turn. As he lifted the gun to the target, he took a very similar stance that, at the time, confused me. I didn't know if he saw it on TV or if airforce security training taught him that, but I was stunned. Seeing it again here was hilarious, and I could not help but laugh. It brought a smile to my face every time I saw it in the intros.  Sir, from all of your testing and 'boring lectures' we have learned so much. You have been a shining light across the community and will be missed greatly. We love you Paul. Semper Fi! Your knowledge, personality, anecdotes, and patient calm delivery have made this channel a space welcoming to everyone from the enthusiast to folks like me.    I mean, I grew up in a family of hunters, but that was about it.  I don't remember anyone talking about home defense as a topic, and I'd hesitate to call any of my family "enthusiasts."  As an adult, I've become an urban dweller in a city frequently reported as being amongst the most dangerous in the United States.  And yet, I've deliberately shied away from firearm ownership.  Not having a piece compels me to be much more aware of my surroundings and conscientious about my decision-making, and I fear that I'd be more likely to get myself into situations I needed a weapon to get out of if I actively carried one.    And yet somehow, the almighty algorithm recommended me this channel several years ago; I'm very glad it did.  I've learned a lot by watching, and I mean that in the most positive way.  I've appreciated seeing someone so thoughtful, so measured, yet so engaging in approach to delivering content on these sorts of topics, from the "new and improved meat target" to the various holiday specials to the very personal anecdotes to the countless surgery beverages and snacks that finally and so ably contributed something useful to society by being shot. Hi Paul, I'm so sorry to hear this.  I've been watching your channel for years and have always enjoyed your content, from gun/ammo testing to anecdotes to holiday cooking/recipes.  Your humor and professionalism in the face of criticism and the vicissitudes of online existence have been inspirational.  I survived (so far!) prostate cancer a couple of years ago and can only begin to empathize with your situation.  I know that open discussion of illness in a public forum can be embarrassing and intrusive, so 'nuff said on that score. Many years ago, one of my favorite college professors announced that he was dying from oral cancer.  The comment of his that has always remained with me is that he intended to face death with the same grace and equanimity with which he'd always tried to face life.  I've always attempted to do the same myself (through bouts with disease, flight testing of homebuilt aircraft, and other less potentially deadly adventures) and I'm confident that you feel the same. All my best to you in this difficult time and to your family. Best regards, Ken

Hi, we're out at my "funeral" today at the Pacific View Memorial Gardens and crematory in Lincoln City, Oregon. Please bear with the sound of mourning in the background. Today, we'll be discussing the difference between being "alive" and as some might say these days, being "un-alive". Now, many of us have a natural predisposition for fearing our own transition into becoming "un-alive", but that fear comes with a couple of caveats. For starters, you'll notice you will save a lot of money on buying groceries once your mortal body ceases to require caloric intake. Secondly, the stress of picking out clothes and getting dressed in the morning is alleviated by the virtue of only needing to wear one outfit for the rest of eternity. Lastly, the metaphysical ability to transcend time and space at will by virtue of slipping through dimensional fissures with your immortal soul really comes in handy when you're sick of paying so much money to fill your gas tank every week. In conclusion, transcendence into "un-aliveness" is mostly a sad occasion for the people left behind rather than the person leaving. With that said, don't try this at home until it's your time to cross over, and thanks for watching the "Paul Harrel leaves the Earthly Realm" video.
